### Camera Protocol Packet Framing Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/doc/camlib_devel.txt

Shows a typical packet structure in camera protocols, featuring designated starting and ending bytes, along with a command byte. This example also includes an ACK byte to confirm successful packet reception.

```pseudocode
Computer: 03 50 00 0f e0 04  // Packet starts with 03, ends with 04
Camera : 03 03 00 3f 03 04  // Another packet with start/end bytes
Computer: 01                 // ACK to confirm reception
```

### Build libgphoto2 with Autoconf

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/README.md

This snippet shows how to build and install libgphoto2 using the Autoconf build system. It includes steps for preparing the build environment, configuring the installation path, and compiling the library. Ensure you have the necessary build tools installed.

```shell
autoreconf -is  # if using a git clone
./configure PKG_CONFIG_PATH="$HOME/.local/lib/pkgconfig${PKG_CONFIG_PATH+:${PKG_CONFIG_PATH}}" --prefix="$HOME/.local"
make
make install
```

### JD11 Camera Serial Command Structure and Examples

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/jd11/jd11.html

This section details the structure of commands sent to and received from the JD11 camera. Commands generally start with 0xFF, followed by an opcode and optional arguments. Responses also typically start with 0xFF.

```text
Command

0xff 0x08

0xff 0xa7

0xff 0xa4

0xff 0xa1

0xff 0xa8

0xff 0xa6

0xff 0xf0

0xff 0xf1

0xff 0xf3

0xff 0x72

0xff 0x73

0xff 0x75

0xff 0x78

0xff 0x79

0xff 0x7a

0xff 0x7b

0xff 0xa9

Arguments

None

None

None

0xff _picturenr_

10 bytes of data ...

None

None

None

None

None

None

None

None.

None

None.

0xff value.

0xff value.

Returns

0xff 0xf1

A packet with between 10 and 20 bytes is returned.

0xff 0x01

0xff 0x01

0xff 0x01

No return expected.

Returns an ASCII hexnumber (starting with two 0x66 ('f'))

Returns 201 or less bytes

Returns 201 or less bytes

0xff 0x71

0xff 0x70/0x71

0xff70 or 0xff71 or something else.

Some data.

0xff 0xXX

Some data.

0xff 0xf1

0xff 0xf1

Description

Ping!s the camera.

3 float factors are returned, they are calculated:  
`f1=r[1]+r[2]*0.1+r[3]*0.01;   f2=r[4]+r[5]*0.1+r[6]*0.01;   f3=r[7]+r[8]*0.1+r[9]*0.01;   `  
Their use is still unknown to me.  
Twain calls it 'LoadGRB'

Select Index Picture to transfer, is followed by packetreading

Selects Image _picturenr_ to transfer. 3 Bytestreams follow (packetreading has to be called 3 times)

Sets the 3 floats. Sends 10 bytes to the camera.  
The bytestream looks: 0xFF A B C D E F G H I  
The floats are: A.BC D.EF G.HI  
A...I are binary values between 0 and 9.  
Twain calls it 'SaveGRB'.

Deletes all images.

Returns the size (in bytes) of the image to transfer next. This command is issued after "select index" or "select image" and is followed by (multiple) packet reads.

The packetreader. It is called in a loop after querying the imagesize. If 201 bytes are read, the 201th byte is the checksum (sum of 0-199)&0xff, otherwise there is no checksum.  
Returns the 200 bytes read.

The packet resend command. Works exactly like the 0xff 0xf1 packetread command, but the last packet is retransmitted. This is useful for corrupted transmissions.

The TestDRAM command according to the Twain drivers. Gets a bool reply.

The TestFLASH command according to the Twain drivers. Gets a bool reply.

The TestADC command according to the Twain drivers. Gets a bool reply.

Appears to take a snapshot and then it should read N packets of data. Strange. There is some text generated and printed into a dialog. I only get back 0xff.  
TWAIN calls it DSC_TestAE.

Function unknown, seems to open/close the shutter in rapid succession.  
TWAIN calls it DSC_AjustAGC.  
Reads reply.

Unclear. GUI enables wait cursor before call and disabled it after.

Unclear.

Set Bulb Mode. Apparently values between 1 and 9.
```

### Get Disks Command and Reply - Protocol Analysis

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/canon/ps350/ps350proto.txt

This section details the byte sequence for the 'get disks' command and its corresponding reply. It highlights the packet structure, including length, command, and total length fields, and provides an example of the reply format for a Windows driver.

```plaintext
00  10  14  00  |  00  00  00  00  |  18  00  01  60  |  14  00  00  00
          <len->                       comm                <---totlen--->
  xx  00  00  00  |  1E  00  00  00
 count

"get disks" reply
-----------------

  00  10  23  00  |  01  00  00  00  |  18  00  22  A0  |  23  00  00  00
          <len->                       comm                <---totlen--->
  xx  00  00  00  |  00  00  00  00  |  52  45  4D  4F  |  56  41  42  4C
 count                                  R   E   M   O      V   A   B   L
  45  5F  31  3A  |  2F  00  00
  E   _   1   :      /

Normally, a string is 0-terminated. I think the second terminating zero
indicates the end of a (possible) list of strings.

After this, the usual EOT/ACK packets follow. I won't indicate this again
below.
```

### libgphoto2: Get Image Commands

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

Similar to thumbnail retrieval, these commands fetch full images. Get Image 1 uses a 6-byte sequence, and Get Image 2 uses a 7-byte sequence ('1B 47 46'). Both involve a 4-byte parameter '<nr>' and expect specific data handling described in the code.

```c
1B 47 <4*nr>                     ESC G xxxx
```

```c
1B 47 46 <4*nr>                  ESC GF xxxx
```

### Start Video Stream using Blink2 Protocol

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/sipix/blink2.txt

Begins the video streaming process, likely initiating ISO transfers. This command is executed via a Blink2 control read.

```protocol
control read 0x4, 0x01, 0x00	-> buf[1]
```

### Camera Protocol ACK/NAK Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/doc/camlib_devel.txt

Demonstrates a basic communication exchange between a computer and a camera using ACK (Acknowledge) and NAK (Negative Acknowledge) bytes. This is a common pattern for confirming packet reception or signaling errors in camera protocols.

```pseudocode
Computer: 01  // Sending ACK
Camera : 01  // Responding with ACK
```

### Frame Guide Mode Control

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/fuji-gfx-100s.txt

Allows reading and writing the frame guide mode setting. This is an enumeration with values 1, 2, and 3.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto/libgphoto2/frame-guide-mode

### Description
Retrieves the current frame guide mode setting of the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto/libgphoto2/frame-guide-mode

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **value** (integer) - The current frame guide mode value.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "value": 1
}
```

## PUT /gphoto/libgphoto2/frame-guide-mode

### Description
Sets the frame guide mode of the camera.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/gphoto/libgphoto2/frame-guide-mode

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **value** (integer) - Required - The desired frame guide mode value (1, 2, or 3).

### Request Example
```json
{
  "value": 2
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **message** (string) - Confirmation of successful update.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "message": "Frame guide mode updated successfully."
}
```
```

### Get Memory Contents using Blink2 Protocol

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/sipix/blink2.txt

Reads specified memory sections from the camera. This involves preparing a buffer with the start address and length, followed by a control write and a bulk read to retrieve the data.

```protocol
Prepare buffer as:
	buf[0..4]	start	(MSB first)
	buf[5..7]	length	(MSB first)

control write 0x0a, 0x03, 0x00, buf[8]
bulk read (length)
```

### Camera Protocol Byte Ordering Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/doc/camlib_devel.txt

Illustrates the concept of 'reverse network order' or little-endian byte ordering, where the least significant byte precedes the most significant byte. This is a common data representation in many communication protocols.

```pseudocode
// '00 08' should be reassembled as '08 00' for correct interpretation.
```

### Get Image Information (libgphoto2 Protocol)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

Retrieves specific information about an image. This command can be issued in two forms, with the latter (ImageInfo 2) having an additional 'F' byte. Both expect a 256-byte data buffer, likely starting with '0x03 0x03'. The exact difference between the two forms is unclear.

```protocol
0x1B 0x49 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X (ESC I xxxx)
```

```protocol
0x1B 0x49 0x46 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X (ESC I F xxxx)
```

### Get Specific Camera Configuration Setting: Image Quality

### SIGMA fp Camera Initialization Sequence with libgphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

This sequence details the steps involved in initializing communication with a SIGMA fp camera using libgphoto2. It outlines specific PTP commands (opcodes), whether they require arguments, and the data exchanged with the camera. This is crucial for understanding how to establish a connection and prepare the camera for further operations like data retrieval or configuration.

```text
Init sequence:
0x9035 no args
	0x9035	recv data from cam: gets an info blob

0x9017	no args	setdatagroup2
	0x9017	send data to cam: 0x03,0x04,0x00,0x04,0x0b

0x9012	no args	getdatagroup1
	0x9012	recv data from cam: 13 ff 7f 58 20 00 01 f8 00 00 01 09 b6 01 01 d0 02 01 00 00 97

0x9013	no args getdatagroup2
	0x9013	recv data from cam: 0e 3f fc 01 02 04 01 00 01 00 00 00 01 01 02 56

0x9014	no args getdatagroup3
	0x9014	recv data from cam: 10 ff a3 00 00 00 01 03 01 00 f0 00 f0 02 05 05 00 a3

0x9018	no args setdatagroup3
	0x9018	send data to cam: 03 00 80 02 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 85

0x9024	no args	setdatagroup4
	0x9024	send data to cam: 03 01 00 02 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 06

0x9034	no args
	0x9034	send data to cam: 15 00 00 00 01 00 00 00 00 00 01 00 01 00 00 00 01 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 1f

0x9033	no args
	0x9033	recv data from cam: d8 ... (0xd8 bytes)

0x9030	no args
	0x9030	recv data from cam: 24 05 00 00 (0x524 bytes)

0x902c	no args	getcamstatus2
	0x902c	recv data from cam: 50 00 00 00 (0x50 bytes)

0x9014	no args getdatagroup3
	0x9014	recv data from cam: 10 ff a3 00 00 00 01 03 01 00 f0 00 f0 02 05 05 02 a5

0x9023	no args	getdatagroup4
	0x9023	recv data from cam: 11 f0 3f 00 03 01 03 ff 0e 00 01 01 01 01 fe 02 02 05 5f

0x9027	no args getdatagroup5
	0x9027	recv data from cam: 0c 2b 00 1e 00 02 00 00 02 88 13 03 01 f8

0x9015	1 arg 0x0	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 00 00 00 00 02 08

0x9015	1 arg 0x1	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 01 00 00 00 00 07

0x9015	1 arg 0x2	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 02 00 00 00 00 08

0x9015	1 arg 0x3	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 03 00 00 00 00 09

0x9015	1 arg 0x4	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 04 00 00 00 00 0a
0x9015	1 arg 0x5	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 05 00 00 00 00 0b

0x9015	1 arg 0x6	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 06 00 00 00 00 0c

0x9015	1 arg 0x7	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 07 00 00 00 00 0d
0x9015	1 arg 0x8	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 08 00 00 00 00 0e
0x9015	1 arg 0x9	getcapturestatus
	0x9015	recv data from cam: 06 09 00 00 00 00 0f
```

### Get Directory Entries using Blink2 Protocol

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/sipix/blink2.txt

Fetches directory entries from the camera. This involves an initial control read to get the number of pictures, followed by a bulk read to retrieve directory information. The buffer format includes movie flags and file start/end times.

```protocol
control read 0x0d, 0x03, 0x00	-> buf[1]
bulk read  (((8*(1+numpics))+0x3f) & ~0x3f) bytes.

Buffer has now: 
i = 0 .. numpics:
	buf[8*(i+1)]	- movie flag
	buf[8*(i+1)+5 ... 7]	- 3 bytes start, MSB first
	buf[8*(i+1)+13 ... 15]	- 3 bytes end, MSB first
```

### Camera Thumbnail Download Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/agfa-cl20/protocol.txt

Presents a sequence of USB commands and a bulk transfer 'in' that appears to be related to downloading a camera thumbnail. The '01 00 00 10 00 14 00 00 00 31 2e 31 36 00 00 00' line is noted as containing new information ('14').

```Assembly
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 00 80 01 00
	answer:		00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 01 00 08 00 00 00
Bulk Transfer "in":
   0000:                   1  .   1  6 
01 00 00 10 00 14 00 00 00 31 2e 31 36 00 00 00   The 14 is new. No idea, what it means...
   0010:       
00 01 00 00 00 00 02 00 00 02 00 00 00 00 06 0a   The 01 could be one of the magic
   0020:                                          numbers, since there was ONE pic
```

### GET /main/settings/fastfs

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-keymission170.txt

Retrieves or sets the fast filesystem setting.

```APIDOC
## GET/SET /main/settings/fastfs

### Description
Retrieves or sets the fast filesystem setting. This is a toggleable option.

### Method
GET/SET

### Endpoint
/main/settings/fastfs

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body (for SET)
- **current** (integer) - The desired state: 0 for off, 1 for on.

### Request Example (SET)
```json
{
  "current": 1
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **current** (integer) - The current state of the fast filesystem (0 for off, 1 for on).

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "current": 1
}
```
```

### Snap Image (libgphoto2)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Initiates an image capture (snap) operation. This command (0x901b) is sent with no arguments and requires a payload specifying the capture mode and amount. The example shows a payload for a single capture.

```c
/* Opcode: 0x901b */
/* Arguments: none */
/* Command: snap */
/* Data to send (example): */
// 0x901b send data to cam: 02  02 01  05
/* Payload interpretation:
   capturemode
   amount
*/
```

### GET Storage Devices

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/ricoh-gr3.txt

Lists and provides details for all storage devices connected to the camera.

```APIDOC
## GET /storage/devices

### Description
Lists and provides details for all storage devices connected to the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/storage/devices

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **storageDevices** (ARRAY) - An array of storage device objects.
  - **storageId** (STRING) - Unique identifier for the storage device.
  - **storageDescription** (STRING) - A description of the storage (e.g., 'SD', 'Builtin RAM').
  - **volumeLabel** (STRING) - The label of the storage volume.
  - **storageType** (STRING) - The type of storage (e.g., 'Removable RAM (memory card)', 'Builtin RAM').
  - **filesystemType** (STRING) - The filesystem type (e.g., 'Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)', 'Generic Hierarchical').
  - **accessCapability** (STRING) - The access capability (e.g., 'Read-Write', 'Read-Only').
  - **maximumCapability** (STRING) - The total capacity of the storage.
  - **freeSpaceBytes** (STRING) - The remaining free space in bytes.
  - **freeSpaceImages** (INTEGER) - The estimated remaining free space in number of images.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "storageDevices": [
    {
      "storageId": "store_00010001",
      "storageDescription": "SD",
      "volumeLabel": "",
      "storageType": "Removable RAM (memory card)",
      "filesystemType": "Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)",
      "accessCapability": "Read-Write",
      "maximumCapability": "127831900160 (121910 MB)",
      "freeSpaceBytes": "110838677504 (105704 MB)",
      "freeSpaceImages": 2077
    },
    {
      "storageId": "store_000f0001",
      "storageDescription": "Software License",
      "volumeLabel": "",
      "storageType": "Builtin RAM",
      "filesystemType": "Generic Hierarchical",
      "accessCapability": "Read-Only",
      "maximumCapability": "1377287 (1 MB)",
      "freeSpaceBytes": "0 (0 MB)",
      "freeSpaceImages": -1
    }
  ]
}
```
```

### GET /main/other/d035 - PTP Property 0xd035

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/olympus-e-m5mark2.txt

## GET /main/other/d035

### Description
Retrieves information about PTP Property 0xd035. This property is of type MENU and is not read-only.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/main/other/d035

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **current_value** (number) - The current setting of the PTP property.
- **choices** (array) - An array of available choices for this property, where each choice is an object with 'index' and 'value'.

#### Response Example
{
  "current_value": 0,
  "choices": [
    {"index": 0, "value": 65529},
    {"index": 1, "value": 65530},
    {"index": 2, "value": 65531},
    ...
  ]
}
```

/* Command to get the configuration descriptor */

/* Example Configuration Descriptor Response: */
/* 0000: 09 02 27 00 01 01 00 80 fa 09 04 01 00 03 ff 00 */
/* 0010: 00 00 07 05 82 02 40 00 00 07 05 03 02 40 00 00 */
/* 0020: 07 05 84 03 01 00 08 */

/* This data describes the power attributes, interfaces, and endpoints. */

### Capture Image Command Example and Error Handling in gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/olympus-tg-620.txt

This snippet demonstrates the use of the `gphoto2 --capture-image` command. It includes the expected output when the camera does not support generic capture, along with detailed error messages and instructions for enabling debugging to help diagnose issues. The example also emphasizes the importance of correct argument quoting.

```bash
#!/bin/bash

# Example command to capture an image
# This command might fail if the camera doesn't support generic capture
gphoto2 --capture-image

# Example of error output when capture fails
# *** Error ***
# Sorry, your camera does not support generic capture
# ERROR: Could not capture image.
# ERROR: Could not capture.
# *** Error (-6: 'Unsupported operation') ***

# Instructions for debugging
# For debugging messages, please use the --debug option.
# env LANG=C gphoto2 --debug --debug-logfile=my-logfile.txt --capture-image

# Note on argument quoting
# Please make sure there is sufficient quoting around the arguments.
```

### Canon PS350/A5 Packet Structure Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/canon/ps350/ps350proto.txt

Illustrates the general structure of a 300-byte packet used in communication. It includes the start byte (0xC0), data bytes, a 2-byte checksum, and the end byte (0xC1). The checksum is a 16-bit CRC calculation.

```text
0xC0  ---296 data bytes---  ---2 byte checksum---  0xC1
```

### Sipix Camera Get Picture Count Request

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/sipix/blink.txt

This USB control request retrieves the number of still images stored on the camera. It's a vendor-specific device-to-host control request. The response contains the picture count in 2 bytes, for example, '04 00' indicates 4 pictures.

```text
bmRequestType=c0 Vendor,device to host
bRequest = 0
wValue = 0
Index = 0
Length = 8

Result:2bytes
contains:04 00
```

--------------------------------

### Protocol Overview

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Details about the host, camera limitations, and basic communication acknowledgments.

```APIDOC
## Protocol Overview

### Host and Camera Limitations
- The PC is always the host.
- Cameras have a maximum of 6 images and 128k of memory.
- Cameras use an image counter for operations.

### Acknowledgments
- ACK = 0x06, NAK = 0x15.
- No ACK/NAK indicates a connection issue.
- Cameras always respond with ACK to sent commands.
- Most commands have a corresponding response.
```

### Luminance Quantization Table Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/polaroid/jpeg.txt

Provides an example of a quantization table for luminance (Table 0) used in JPEG compression. It shows the 8x8 matrix of values that are used as multipliers for the 8x8 DCT coefficient blocks.

```text
16  11  10  16  24  40  51  61
12  12  14  19  26  58  60  55
14  13  16  24  40  57  69  56
14  17  22  29  51  87  80  62
18  22  37  56  68 109 103  77
24  35  55  64  81 104 113  92
49  64  78  87 103 121 120 101
72  92  95  98 112 100 103  99
```

### libgphoto2 Read-Only Enumeration Property Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-d5100.txt

Shows a read-only enumeration property. This example indicates a property that can be changed but is currently set to a default value and cannot be modified by the user.

```text
Change Pic Ctrl Item(0xd201):(read only) (type=0x4) Enumeration [] value: 0
```

--------------------------------

### Command Packet Structure

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Defines the structure of a command packet sent from the host to the camera. It starts with a start byte (0x02), followed by the command, optional data, and ends with an end byte (0x03).

```text
[0x02] [COMMAND] [DATA] [DATA] [...] [0x03]
```

### List All Camera Configurations with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sony-nex6.txt

This command lists all configurable parameters of the connected camera. The output is redirected to a file named 'config.txt'. This is useful for understanding the camera's settings and available options.

```bash
gphoto2 --list-all-config >config.txt
more config.txt
```

### libgphoto2: Command P (Set Configuration)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

This command, cmd_P, is used to set configuration parameters on the camera. It writes an 11-byte sequence and expects a 1-byte NACK or 1024-byte data response. The specific meaning of 'nr1' and 'nr2' requires further investigation.

```c
1B 50 46 <nr1><nr1><nr1><nr1> <nr2><nr2><nr2><nr2>        ESC P F xxxxyyyy
```

### Sync Translations with TranslationProject

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/RELEASE-HOWTO.md

This command synchronizes translation files from the translation project repository to the local libgphoto2 project. It uses rsync to fetch the latest translations for libgphoto2, libgphoto2_port, and optionally gphoto2 itself. Ensure you have the necessary permissions and network access to the translationproject.org server.

```shell
rsync -Lrtvz  translationproject.org::tp/latest/libgphoto2/  po
rsync -Lrtvz  translationproject.org::tp/latest/libgphoto2_port/  libgphoto2_port/po

# If gphoto2 is released too:
rsync -Lrtvz  translationproject.org::tp/latest/gphoto2/  po
```

### SetupPacket Data Analysis in libgphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/agfa-cl20/protocol.txt

This section documents various 'SetupPacket' transmissions observed in the libgphoto2 project. These packets appear to control camera settings or initiate operations. The varied byte sequences suggest different command types or parameters being sent to the camera. No specific programming language is implied, as this represents raw data.

```text
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 00 80 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 00 80 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 00 80 01 00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 01 00 0d 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 20 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : 41 02 00 00 07 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 01 00 00 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : 41 02 00 00 07 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 00 00 00 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : 41 02 00 00 07 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 00 00 01 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 85 89 01 00
SetupPacket          : 41 0a 01 00 00 00 00 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
SetupPacket          : c1 00 00 00 21 05 01 00
```

### Menu and Configuration API

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-d7100.txt

Interact with camera menus and configuration settings, including retrieving current values and available choices for various properties.

```APIDOC
## GET /camera/config/{config_path}

### Description
Retrieves the configuration details for a specific menu or setting path on the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/camera/config/{config_path}

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **config_path** (string) - Required - The path to the configuration item (e.g., `/main/other/d1b2`).

### Request Example
```json
{
  "method": "GET",
  "endpoint": "/camera/config/main/other/d1b2"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **label** (string) - The human-readable label for the configuration item.
- **type** (string) - The type of the configuration item (e.g., MENU, RANGE).
- **current** (string or number) - The current value of the configuration item.
- **choices** (array) - An array of available choices for MENU type items, each with a `value` and `label`.
- **bottom** (number) - The minimum value for RANGE type items.
- **top** (number) - The maximum value for RANGE type items.
- **step** (number) - The step increment for RANGE type items.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "label": "Info Display Error Status",
  "type": "MENU",
  "current": 0,
  "choices": [
    {
      "value": 0,
      "label": "0"
    },
    {
      "value": 1,
      "label": "1"
    }
  ]
}
```

## PUT /camera/config/{config_path}

### Description
Sets a new value for a specific menu or configuration item on the camera.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/camera/config/{config_path}

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **config_path** (string) - Required - The path to the configuration item (e.g., `/main/other/d1b2`).

#### Request Body
- **value** (string or number) - Required - The new value to set for the configuration item.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "method": "PUT",
  "endpoint": "/camera/config/main/other/d1b2",
  "value": 1
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **message** (string) - Confirmation message indicating the setting was updated.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "message": "Configuration updated successfully."
}
```
```

### SetupPacket for Image Information Retrieval

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/agfa-cl20/protocol2.txt

These SetupPackets are used to request information for each picture. The commands vary depending on whether a flash card is used ('flash card') or not ('no flash card'). The first byte '41' is consistent, but subsequent bytes differ, indicating different communication modes or data structures.

```text
flash-card: 41 0a 01 00 08 00 00 00
no flash card: 41 03 ff 0f 00 00 00 00

flash-card: 41 0a 02 00 08 00 00 00
no flash card: 41 03 fe 0f 00 00 00 00

flash-card: 41 0a 03 00 08 00 00 00
no flash card: 41 03 fd 0f 00 00 00 00

flash-card: 41 0a 04 00 08 00 00 00
no flash card: 41 03 fc 0f 00 00 00 00

flash-card: 41 0a 05 00 08 00 00 00
no flash card: 41 03 fb 0f 00 00 00 00
```

--------------------------------

### Storage Devices Summary

## Storage Devices Summary

### Description

### Storage Device: store_00020002
- **StorageDescription**: Card
- **VolumeLabel**: SAMSUNG Digital Camera-nnnnnnnnn-20002
- **Storage Type**: Removable RAM (memory card)
- **Filesystemtype**: Generic Hierarchical
- **Access Capability**: Read-Write
- **Maximum Capability**: 63247089664 (60317 MB)
- **Free Space (Bytes)**: 57135595520 (54488 MB)
- **Free Space (Images)**: -1
```

### Storage Device Information

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-coolpix7600.txt

Get details about the storage devices available on the camera.

```APIDOC
## GET /storage/summary

### Description
Retrieves a summary of the storage devices connected to the camera, including details like storage type, filesystem, and available space.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/storage/summary

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **storage_id** (string) - Identifier for the storage device (e.g., store_00010001).
- **storage_description** (string) - Description of the storage (e.g., None).
- **volume_label** (string) - The label of the storage volume.
- **storage_type** (string) - The type of storage (e.g., Removable RAM (memory card)).
- **filesystem_type** (string) - The filesystem type of the storage (e.g., Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)).
- **access_capability** (string) - The access capability of the storage (e.g., Read-Write).
- **maximum_capability_bytes** (integer) - The maximum capacity of the storage in bytes.
- **free_space_bytes** (integer) - The amount of free space on the storage in bytes.
- **free_space_images** (integer) - The estimated number of images that can be stored in the free space.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "store_00010001": {
    "storage_description": "None",
    "volume_label": "None",
    "storage_type": "Removable RAM (memory card)",
    "filesystem_type": "Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)",
    "access_capability": "Read-Write",
    "maximum_capability_bytes": 1005696,
    "free_space_bytes": 1017413632,
    "free_space_images": 287
  }
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### Prepare for Dir Download Command and Reply - Protocol Analysis

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/canon/ps350/ps350proto.txt

This section outlines the protocol for preparing a directory download. It provides the byte structure for the 'prepare for dir download' command, which includes a sector identifier, and its corresponding reply, indicating readiness for the subsequent download.

```plaintext
"prepare for dir download" command
----------------------------------

  00  10  14  00  |  00  00  00  00  |  04  00  01  60  |  14  00  00  00
          <len->                       comm                <---totlen--->
  xx  00  00  00  |  xx  xx  xx  xx
 count               <---sector--->

This command is sent to indicate that a dir download will follow.

(I speak of "download" because I see the camera as "information server".)


"prepare for dir download" reply
--------------------------------

  00  10  14  00  |  01  00  00  00  |  04  00  02  60  |  14  00  00  00
          <len->                       comm                <---totlen--->
  xx  00  00  00  |  00  00  00  00
 count

```

### GET /camera/settings

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-d7500.txt

Retrieves the current values and available options for all configurable camera settings.

```APIDOC
## GET /camera/settings

### Description
Retrieves the current values and available options for all configurable camera settings.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/camera/settings

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **settings** (object) - An object containing all camera settings.
  - **setting_id** (object) - Details for a specific setting.
    - **label** (string) - The human-readable label for the setting.
    - **type** (string) - The type of setting (e.g., 'MENU', 'RANGE', 'TEXT').
    - **current** (string|number) - The current value of the setting.
    - **choices** (array) - (For MENU type) An array of available choices.
      - **value** (string|number) - The internal value of the choice.
      - **label** (string) - The human-readable label of the choice.
    - **bottom** (number) - (For RANGE type) The minimum allowed value.
    - **top** (number) - (For RANGE type) The maximum allowed value.
    - **step** (number) - (For RANGE type) The increment step for the value.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "settings": {
    "/main/other/d152": {
      "label": "Tune Preset 1",
      "type": "RANGE",
      "current": 612,
      "bottom": 0,
      "top": 1224,
      "step": 1
    },
    "/main/other/d158": {
      "label": "PTP Property 0xd158",
      "type": "MENU",
      "current": 0,
      "choices": [
        {"value": 0, "label": "0"},
        {"value": 1, "label": "1"}
      ]
    },
    "/main/other/d1a4": {
      "label": "Live View Prohibit Condition",
      "type": "TEXT",
      "current": "0"
    }
  }
}
```
```

### Config API (GetCamCanSetInfo5)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Retrieves configuration information from the camera, detailing parameters that can be set. Returns a structured list of configurable settings.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto2/config

### Description
Fetches configuration settings from the camera that can be modified. Provides a structured list of settable parameters and their properties.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto2/config

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **configuration** (array) - An array of configuration objects, each detailing a settable parameter:
  - **tag** (hex) - The tag identifier for the configuration parameter.
  - **type** (hex) - The data type of the parameter.
  - **elements** (integer) - The number of elements.
  - **value** (hex) - The current or default value of the parameter.
  - **ascii_value** (string) - The ASCII representation of the parameter value if applicable.

### Response Example
```json
{
  "configuration": [
    {
      "tag": "0x0001",
      "type": "0x0002",
      "elements": 9,
      "value": "0x0000003c",
      "ascii_value": "SIGMA fp"
    }
  ]
}
```
```

### libgphoto2 Command Reference (Q-T)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Details the commands from 'Q' to 'T' for the libgphoto2 protocol. Includes command data bytes, response data bytes, and a description of the command's function.

```text
CMD	CMD DATA BYTES		RESP DATA BYTES		Description
---	-----------------------	---------------------	-----------------------
Q	1 (video mode)			1 (0)			video mode (!!)
								(requires capture card)
R	1 (register index)		1 (register value)	read register value
						  (error = 0xFF)
T	2 (min, max)			1 (0)			set exposure threshold
```

### Chrominance Quantization Table Example

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/polaroid/jpeg.txt

Presents an example of a quantization table for chrominance (Table 1) used in JPEG compression. Similar to the luminance table, it's an 8x8 matrix that scales DCT coefficients, with higher values indicating less precision for chroma information.

```text
17  18  24  47  99  99  99  99
18  21  26  66  99  99  99  99
24  26  56  99  99  99  99  99
47  66  99  99  99  99  99  99
99  99  99  99  99  99  99  99
99  99  99  99  99  99  99  99
99  99  99  99  99  99  99  99
99  99  99  99  99  99  99  99
```

### PTP Supported Operations - libgphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sony-qx30u.txt

Lists the PTP operations supported by the device, categorized by standard PTP operations and vendor-specific ones. This includes fundamental operations like Get device info, Open session, Close session, and specific operations related to Sony's PTP extensions such as qx_getallpropertydata and qx_setpropvalB. Understanding these is vital for device control.

```text
Supported operations:
  0x1001 (Get device info)
  0x1002 (Open session)
  0x1003 (Close session)
  0x1004 (Get storage IDs)
  0x1005 (Get storage info)
  0x1006 (Get number of objects)
  0x1007 (Get object handles)
  0x1008 (Get object info)
  0x1009 (Get object)
  0x100a (Get thumbnail)
  0x101b (Get partial object)

  0x967d (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x96f1 (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x96f5 (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x96f6 (Unknown PTP_OC)	qx_getallpropertydata
  0x96f8 (Unknown PTP_OC)	qx_setpropvalB
  0x96fa (Unknown PTP_OC)	qx_setpropvalA
  0x96fd (Unknown PTP_OC)	qx_getproperties
  0x96fe (Unknown PTP_OC)	qx_connect

  0x9801 (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x9802 (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x9803 (Unknown PTP_OC)
  0x9805 (Unknown PTP_OC)
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2 Coding Style Example (C)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/HACKING.md

This C code example demonstrates the libgphoto2 coding style, including multi-line and single-line comments, function structure, variable declarations, error checking with `gp_`-functions, and the use of macros like `CHECK_RESULT`. It also shows a switch statement for handling error codes.

```c
int
my_func (int arg)
{
	int var, res;

	/*
	 * This is a multiline
	 * comment. Use TAB for
	 * indentation!
	 */
	res = gp_some_action (var);

	/* This is a simple one-line comment */
	if (res < 0) {
		gp_log (GP_LOG_DEBUG, "Error happened!");

		/* Note that we _don't_ indent the case statements */
		switch (res) {
		case GP_ERROR:
			gp_log (GP_LOG_DEBUG, "Generic error");
			break;
		default:
			gp_log (GP_LOG_DEBUG, "Not a generic error");
		}
		return (res);
	}

	return (GP_OK);
}

```

### USB Configuration Selection Command (libgphoto2)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/agfa-cl20/protocol2.txt

This shows the command used to select a specific configuration for the camera. The example selects configuration 0x01, with the direction set to 'out' and a length of 0x0000.

```C
/* Command to select configuration 0x01 */
/* Direction is 'out' (00) */
/* Length is 0x0000 (00 00) */
/* SetupPacket          : 00 09 01 00 00 00 00 00 */

/* After this command, the camera should be ready for further communication. */
```

### Get Camera Capability Info 5 (libgphoto2)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Retrieves detailed capability information for the camera. This command (0x9030) returns a structured list of properties, including their tags, data types, element counts, and values. This information is crucial for understanding the camera's supported features and parameters.

```text
/* Opcode: 0x9030 */
/* Command: GetCamCanSetInfo5 */
/* Response structure (example entries): */
/* ptp                         (2): entry 0: tag=0x0001, type=0x0001, elements=5, value=0x00000420 */
/* ptp                         (2): entry 1: tag=0x0002, type=0x0001, elements=3, value=0x00010203 */
/* ptp                         (2): entry 2: tag=0x0003, type=0x0001, elements=4, value=0x00630001 */
/* ptp                         (2): entry 3: tag=0x0004, type=0x0008, elements=3, value=0x00000425 */
/* ... additional entries up to entry 19 ... */
```

### libgphoto2 Command Reference (M-P)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

```text
CMD	CMD DATA BYTES		RESP DATA BYTES		Description
---	-----------------------	---------------------	-----------------------
M	1 (0)				hdr+pixel data+info	upload thumbnail (increments
									image counter & image index)
P	1 (new port value)		1 (old port value)	set port value
```

### List and Get Camera Configuration Options with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-coolpix5400.txt

This command sequence first lists all available configuration options for the camera and then, for each option, retrieves its current setting. This is useful for understanding the camera's adjustable parameters and their current states. It involves piping the output of '--list-config' to a 'while read' loop, which then executes '--get-config' for each identified setting.

```bash
gphoto2 --list-config  |while read x; do echo $x ; gphoto2 --get-config $x ; done
```

### Attempt Image Capture with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/fuji-finepix-s8600.txt

This command attempts to capture an image from the connected camera. If the camera does not support generic capture operations via gphoto2, an error message will be displayed indicating the unsupported operation.

```bash
~$ gphoto2 --capture-image
RESULTS
----------------------------------------------------------------

*** Error ***
Sorry, your camera does not support generic capture
ERROR: Could not capture image.
ERROR: Could not capture.
*** Error (-6: 'Unsupported operation') ***
```

### GET /main/imgsettings/whitebalance

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-keymission170.txt

Retrieves or sets the white balance setting.

```APIDOC
## GET/SET /main/imgsettings/whitebalance

### Description
Retrieves or sets the white balance setting for images.

### Method
GET/SET

### Endpoint
/main/imgsettings/whitebalance

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body (for SET)
- **current** (string) - The desired white balance mode. Accepted values include 'Automatic', 'Daylight', 'Tungsten', 'Fluorescent', 'Unknown value 1001'.

### Request Example (SET)
```json
{
  "current": "Daylight"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **current** (string) - The current white balance mode.
- **choices** (array of strings) - Available white balance modes.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "current": "Automatic",
  "choices": [
    "Automatic",
    "Daylight",
    "Tungsten",
    "Fluorescent",
    "Unknown value 1001"
  ]
}
```
```

### Get Camera Summary with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/samsung-nx01.txt

The --summary option retrieves a comprehensive overview of the camera's status, including manufacturer, model, capture/display formats, device capabilities, storage information, and device properties. The output can be redirected to a file.

```bash
localhost: ~$ gphoto2 --summary >summary.txt
Camera summary:
Manufacturer: SAMSUNG Electronics Co. Ltd. 
Model: SAMSUNG NX1
  Version: V1.0

Capture Formats: Unknown(0000)
Display Formats: Unknown(b984), Unknown(b982), MP3, Unknown(b901), Unknown(b981), JPEG, Association/Directory, Unknown(ba05), Unknown(b906), Undefined Type, GIF, BMP, PNG, MS Wave, MS AVI, MPEG, ASF, Unknown(ba03)

Device Capabilities:
	File Download, File Deletion, File Upload
	No Image Capture, No Open Capture, No vendor specific capture

Storage Devices Summary:
store_00020001:
	StorageDescription: Card
	VolumeLabel: -20001
	Storage Type: Removable RAM (memory card)
	Filesystemtype: Generic Hierarchical
	Access Capability: Read-Write
	Maximum Capability: 15923150848 (15185 MB)
	Free Space (Bytes): 15464103936 (14747 MB)
	Free Space (Images): -1

Device Property Summary:
Battery Level(0x5001):cannot be queried.
Property 0xd401:cannot be queried.
Property 0xd402:cannot be queried.
Property 0xd404:cannot be queried.
Property 0xd407:cannot be queried.

```

### Capture Formats

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-coolpix-p1000.txt

Get a list of supported image capture and display formats for the camera.

```APIDOC

### Description
Retrieves the supported capture and display formats of the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/api/camera/formats

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **capture_formats** (array of strings) - Supported formats for capturing images.
- **display_formats** (array of strings) - Supported formats for displaying images.

#### Response Example
{
  "capture_formats": ["JPEG"],
  "display_formats": ["Undefined Type", "Association/Directory", "Script", "DPOF", "MPEG", "Defined Type", "JPEG", "JFIF"]
}

### DRangeOptimize Configuration

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sony-rx100m7.txt

Allows setting and getting the DRangeOptimize setting of the camera. This is a MENU type property.

```APIDOC
## GET /main/other/d201

### Description
Retrieves the current DRangeOptimize setting of the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/main/other/d201

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **current** (integer) - The current DRangeOptimize value. See choices for possible values.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "current": 31
}
```

## PUT /main/other/d201

### Description
Sets the DRangeOptimize setting of the camera. Use one of the available choice values.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/main/other/d201

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **value** (integer) - Required - The desired DRangeOptimize value. Possible values include: 0 (1), 1 (31), 2 (17), etc.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "value": 1
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **message** (string) - Indicates success or failure of the operation.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "message": "DRangeOptimize set successfully"
}
```
```

### GET /gphoto/libgphoto2/device/info

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/canon-eos-r100.txt

Retrieves comprehensive information about the connected camera device.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto/libgphoto2/device/info

### Description
Fetches detailed information about the connected camera, including its manufacturer, model, serial number, firmware version, supported formats, capabilities, storage details, and PTP operations.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto/libgphoto2/device/info

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **manufacturer** (string) - The manufacturer of the camera.
- **model** (string) - The model name of the camera.
- **version** (string) - The firmware version of the camera.
- **serial_number** (string) - The unique serial number of the camera.
- **vendor_extension_id** (string) - The ID of the vendor extension.
- **capture_formats** (array of strings) - List of supported capture formats (e.g., JPEG).
- **display_formats** (array of strings) - List of supported display formats.
- **device_capabilities** (array of strings) - List of general device capabilities (e.g., File Download, File Upload).
- **storage_devices** (object) - Summary of storage devices connected to the camera.
  - **store_id** (string) - Identifier for the storage device.
  - **storage_description** (string) - Description of the storage medium (e.g., SD).
  - **volume_label** (string) - The volume label of the storage.
  - **storage_type** (string) - Type of storage (e.g., Removable RAM).
  - **filesystem_type** (string) - The filesystem type used on the storage.
  - **access_capability** (string) - Read/Write access capability.
  - **maximum_capability** (string) - Total capacity of the storage in bytes and MB.
  - **free_space_bytes** (string) - Free space on the storage in bytes and MB.
  - **free_space_images** (string) - Free space indicated in number of images.
- **device_properties** (array of objects) - List of device properties.
  - **id** (string) - Property identifier (e.g., 0xd402).
  - **access** (string) - Access type (read only, readwrite).
  - **type** (string) - Data type of the property.
  - **name** (string) - Name of the property (e.g., 'Canon EOS R100').
  - **value** (any) - Current value of the property.
  - **enum_values** (array of any) - Possible enumerated values for the property (if applicable).
- **ptp_operations** (array of strings) - List of supported PTP operations by their hexadecimal codes and names.

#### Response Example
```json

### Get Camera Information (-INFO)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ricoh/g3.txt

Retrieves information about a folder or file, including byte size, width, height, and K-value. The command format is -INFO folder/file.

```text
-INFO folder/file	- 200 %d byte W=%d H=%d K=%d for -INFO
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2: Command V (Set Parameter)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

Commands cmd_V 1 and cmd_V 2 are used to set parameters. cmd_V 1 writes a 6-byte sequence, while cmd_V 2 writes a 7-byte sequence. Both expect a 1-byte NACK/ACK response. The parameter 'xxxx' is a 4-byte value.

```c
1B 56 <nr> <nr> <nr> <nr>        ESC V xxxx
```

```c
1B 56 46 <nr> <nr> <nr> <nr>     ESC V F xxxx
```

--------------------------------

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2: Command K (Unknown Function)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

Commands cmd_K 1 and cmd_K 2 are marked as UNSUPPORTED. They involve writing 6 or 7 bytes respectively, with cmd_K 2 appending '46'. Both expect a 1-byte NACK/ACK response, and 'xxxx' is a 4-byte parameter.

```c
1B 4B <nr> <nr> <nr> <nr>        ESC K xxxx
```

```c
1B 4B 46 <nr> <nr> <nr> <nr>     ESC K xxxx
```

### Standard gphoto2 Camera Interface

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/canon/doc/canon-sections.txt

Defines the standard interface for interacting with cameras using gphoto2. The `clear_readiness` function is part of this interface and is declared in library.h.

```c
#include "library.h"

// Function to clear camera readiness status
void reset_camera_readiness(Camera *camera) {
    clear_readiness(camera);
}
```

--------------------------------

### GET Capture Formats

--------------------------------

### Navigating Camera Memory for Photo Download (MR97310)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/mars/protocol.txt

Illustrates the process of moving the camera's internal memory pointer to a specific location, such as the start of the first photo at memory block 0x400. This involves a series of command and read requests.

```text
1. Send '19 0f' to prepare for memory location change.
2. Send '21', read response.
3. Send '19 00' to specify the memory block.
4. Send '21', read response.
5. Send '19 04' to specify the offset.
6. Send '21', read response repeatedly until the first byte of the response is '0x0a', indicating the pointer is set.
```

### Initiate Full Image Download Command

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/dimera/Protocol.txt

The '71' command, along with '59', is used to download full-resolution images. The response to '71' provides header information similar to the thumbnail download. It's hypothesized that '71' might be an inquiry command, while '59' prepares the camera for the actual download, which can take a significant amount of time.

```hex
71 <image number> 00
```

--------------------------------

### JPEG Start of Frame 0 Structure

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/polaroid/jpeg.txt

Details the 'Start of Frame 0' marker (0xFF C0), specifying its length, bits per pixel, image dimensions (height and width), and component information. It outlines the structure of a component set, including its identifier and vertical/horizontal compression ratio.

```text
0xFF 0xC0 0x00 length bits-per-pixel 0x00 height(2 bytes) width(2 bytes)
#_of_components sets(1 or 3 of them)
A set would be component# v/h quantization-table-number.
```

--------------------------------

### Mars MR97310 Camera Initialization and Command Sequences

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/mars/protocol.txt

Lists observed command sequences used for initializing the camera, managing memory pointers, and confirming data transfers. These sequences are crucial for correctly interacting with the camera's internal state.

```text
19 51: Starts initialization, data download, and exit sequences.
19 b5: Appears during initialization, possibly related to memory addresses.
19 0f: Instructs to move to a memory location.
19 54: Computer's acknowledgement of successful data download.
19 ba: Flag to reset memory location on exit, followed by reset instructions.
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2 Command Reference (U-X)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Details the commands from 'U' to 'X' for the libgphoto2 protocol. Includes command data bytes, response data bytes, and a description of the command's function.

```text
CMD	CMD DATA BYTES		RESP DATA BYTES		Description
---	-----------------------	---------------------	-----------------------
U	1 (0)				hdr+pixel data+info	upload image
V	1 (0)				version string		get version information
W	2 (register index, value)	1 (0 = OK, 0xFF = ERR)	write register value
X	1 (0)				2 (min, max)		get exposure threshold
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2: Upload Command

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

The Upload command is initiated by sending a 2-byte sequence: '1B 55'. The subsequent data transfer and expected response are detailed within the associated code.

```c
1B 55                            ESC U
```

--------------------------------

### Storage Devices

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-coolpix-p1000.txt

Get information about the storage devices connected to the camera, including capacity and free space.

```APIDOC
## GET /api/storage

### Description
Retrieves information about the storage devices connected to the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/api/storage

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **storage_devices** (array of objects) - A list of storage devices with their properties.
  - **id** (string) - Identifier for the storage device (e.g., store_00010001).
  - **storage_description** (string) - Description of the storage.
  - **volume_label** (string) - The label of the storage volume.
  - **storage_type** (string) - Type of storage (e.g., Removable RAM (memory card)).
  - **filesystem_type** (string) - The filesystem type (e.g., Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)).
  - **access_capability** (string) - Read/Write capability.
  - **maximum_capability** (string) - Total storage capacity.
  - **free_space_bytes** (string) - Free space in bytes.
  - **free_space_images** (string) - Estimated free space in images.

#### Response Example
{
  "storage_devices": [
    {
      "id": "store_00010001",
      "storage_description": "None",
      "volume_label": "None",
      "storage_type": "Removable RAM (memory card)",
      "filesystem_type": "Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)",
      "access_capability": "Read-Write",
      "maximum_capability": "127831900160 (121910 MB)",
      "free_space_bytes": "118681370624 (113183 MB)",
      "free_space_images": "25151"
    }
  ]
}
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2 Command Reference (A-E)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Details the commands from 'A' to 'E' for the libgphoto2 protocol. Includes command data bytes, response data bytes, and a description of the command's function.

```text
CMD	CMD DATA BYTES		RESP DATA BYTES		Description
---	-----------------------	---------------------	-----------------------
A	1 (index #)			1 (0)			move to image index #
B	2 (duration, num times)		1 (0)			beep (duration*50ms)
E	1 (test char)			1 (test char)		echo (test or wake up camera)
```

--------------------------------

### Get Camera View Frame (libgphoto2)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Initiates a live view stream from the camera. This command (0x902b) is sent with no arguments and is used to obtain a real-time video feed, often for preview purposes before capturing an image.

```c
/* Opcode: 0x902b */
/* Arguments: none */
/* Command: getcamviewframe */
// This command typically initiates a stream of image data.
```

```APIDOC
## GET /camera/storage

### Description
Retrieves a summary of storage devices available on the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/camera/storage

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **storage_devices** (array<object>) - A list of storage devices.
  - **storage_description** (string) - Description of the storage.
  - **volume_label** (string) - The volume label of the storage.
  - **storage_type** (string) - The type of storage (e.g., Builtin RAM).
  - **filesystem_type** (string) - The filesystem type.
  - **access_capability** (string) - Read/Write capability.
  - **maximum_capability_mb** (number) - Maximum storage capacity in MB.
  - **free_space_bytes** (number) - Free space in bytes.
  - **free_space_mb** (number) - Free space in MB.
  - **free_space_images** (number) - Free space in terms of number of images.

#### Response Example

  "storage_devices": [
    {
      "storage_description": "None",
      "volume_label": "V",

      "maximum_capability_mb": 0,
      "free_space_bytes": 0,
      "free_space_mb": 0,
      "free_space_images": -1
    }
  ]
}
```

### Get Specific Camera Configuration Setting: Capture Target

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-coolpix5400.txt

This command retrieves the current capture target setting, showing whether images are being saved to Internal RAM or a Memory card. It also lists the available choices. This illustrates how to get the current selection and options for a RADIO type setting.

```bash
# gphoto2 --get-config /main/settings/capturetarget
Label: Capture Target                                          
Type: RADIO
Current: Internal RAM
Choice: 0 Internal RAM
Choice: 1 Memory card
```

### GET /gphoto/libgphoto2/properties

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-s2.txt

Retrieves a list of all available camera properties with their current values, types, and capabilities.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto/libgphoto2/properties

### Description
Retrieves a list of all available camera properties with their current values, types, and capabilities.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto/libgphoto2/properties

### Parameters
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **properties** (array of objects) - A list of camera properties.
  - **id** (string) - The unique identifier for the property (e.g., "0xf00d").
  - **label** (string) - The human-readable name of the property (e.g., "Long Exposure Noise Reduction").
  - **access** (string) - The access level for the property ("readwrite" or "readonly").
  - **type** (integer) - The data type of the property.
  - **range** (object, optional) - The valid range for numerical properties.
    - **min** (number) - The minimum value.
    - **max** (number) - The maximum value.
    - **step** (number) - The step increment.
  - **enumeration** (array of integers/strings, optional) - The list of possible values for enumeration types.
  - **current_value** (number/string) - The current value of the property.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "properties": [
    {
      "id": "0xf00d",
      "label": "Long Exposure Noise Reduction",
      "access": "readwrite",
      "type": 2,
      "range": {
        "min": 0,
        "max": 1,
        "step": 1
      },
      "current_value": 0
    },
    {
      "id": "0xf00e",
      "label": "High ISO Noise Reduction",
      "access": "readwrite",
      "type": 2,
      "enumeration": [0, 3],
      "current_value": 0
    }
    // ... more properties
  ]
}
```
```

### Get Camera Summary with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-d3200.txt

The `gphoto2 --summary` command retrieves a comprehensive overview of the connected camera's status, capabilities, storage information, and configurable properties. This is useful for understanding the camera's features and current state. It requires the `gphoto2` utility and a connected camera.

```bash
gphoto2 --summary
Camera summary:
Manufacturer: Nikon Corporation
Model: D3200
  Version: V1.00
  Serial Number: nnnnnnn0000000000000000000000000
Vendor Extension ID: 0xa (1.0)
Vendor Extension Description: microsoft.com: 1.0

Display Formats: JPEG, Undefined Type, Association/Directory, DPOF, Script,
Apple Quicktime

Device Capabilities:
File Download, File Deletion, File Upload
Generic Image Capture, No Open Capture, No vendor specific capture

Storage Devices Summary:
store_00010001:
StorageDescription: None
VolumeLabel: EOS_DIGITAL [Slot 1]
Storage Type: Removable RAM (memory card)
Filesystemtype: Digital Camera Layout (DCIM)
Access Capability: Read Only with Object deletion
Maximum Capability: 16138633216 (15391 MB)
Free Space (Bytes): 12849348608 (12254 MB)
Free Space (Images): 823

Device Property Summary:
Battery Level(0x5001):(read only) (type=0x2) Range [0 - 100, step 1] value: 35%
(35)

'6016x4000',
'4512x3000',
'3008x2000'
] value: '6016x4000'

F-Number(0x5007):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [500,560,630,710,800,900,1000,1100,1300,1400,1600,1800,2000,2200,2500,2900,3200] value: f/5 (500)
Focal Length(0x5008):(read only) (type=0x6) Range [1800 - 5500, step 1] value: 34 mm (3400)
Focus Mode(0x500a):(read only) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,32784,32785,32786,32787] value: AF-A (32786)
Exposure Metering Mode(0x500b):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [2,3,4] value: Multi-spot (3)
Flash Mode(0x500c):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [4,32784,32785,32786,32787] value: Auto (32784)
Exposure Time(0x500d):(read only) (type=0x6) Enumeration [2,3,4,5,6,8,10,12,15,20,25,31,40,50,62,80,100,125,166,200,250,333,400,500,666,769,1000,1250,1666,2000,2500,3333,4000,5000,6250,7692,10000,13000,16000,20000,25000,30000,40000,50000,60000,80000,100000,130000,150000,200000,250000,300000] value: 0.017 sec (1666)
Exposure Program Mode(0x500e):(read only) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2,3,4,32784,32785,32786,32787,32788,32789,32790,32791] value: A (3)
Exposure Index (film speed ISO)(0x500f):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [100,200,400,800,1600,3200,6400,12800] value: ISO 400 (400)
Exposure Bias Compensation(0x5010):(readwrite) (type=0x3) Enumeration [-5000,-4666,-4333,-4000,-3666,-3333,-3000,-2666,-2333,-2000,-1666,-1333,-1000,-666,-333,0,333,666,1000,1333,1666,2000,2333,2666,3000,3333,3666,4000,4333,4666,5000] value: 0.0 stops (0)
Date & Time(0x5011):(readwrite) (type=0xffff) '20130531T143650'

### Attempt Camera Preview Capture with gphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/nikon-d3200.txt

This command attempts to capture a preview from the camera. It requires the `gphoto2` utility and can optionally include debug logging. The output indicates success or failure, such as the camera not supporting LiveView mode. Dependencies include the `gphoto2` library and a connected camera.

```bash
env LANG=C gphoto2 --debug --debug-logfile=D3100-logifle.txt --capture-preview

*** Error ***
Sorry, your Nikon camera does not support LiveView mode
*** Error (-6: 'Unsupported operation') ***
```

--------------------------------

### GET /gphoto2/device/capabilities

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/canon-eos760d.txt

Lists the capabilities of the connected camera, such as file operations, capture modes, and connectivity features.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto2/device/capabilities

### Description
Lists the capabilities of the connected camera, such as file operations, capture modes, and connectivity features.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto2/device/capabilities

### Parameters

None

### Request Example

None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **file_operations** (array of strings) - Supported file operations (e.g., "File Download", "File Deletion", "File Upload").
- **capture_modes** (array of strings) - Supported image capture modes (e.g., "No Image Capture", "Canon EOS Capture").
- **connectivity** (array of strings) - Supported connectivity features (e.g., "Canon Wifi support").

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "file_operations": [
    "File Download",
    "File Deletion",
    "File Upload"
  ],

### libgphoto2 Command Reference (G-I)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/barbie/Protocol.txt

Details the commands from 'G' to 'I' for the libgphoto2 protocol. Includes command data bytes, response data bytes, and a description of the command's function.

```text
CMD	CMD DATA BYTES		RESP DATA BYTES		Description
---	-----------------------	---------------------	-----------------------
G	1 (delay & retry flags)		1 (0, use grab image	grab image - increments counter,
					  result for error	lower nibble = self timer delay,
								upper nibble = retry numbers
								0,16,32,64(force),112
I	1 (0)				1 (image index)		get image counter
								(use reset first to get # pics)
```

### Get Big Partial Picture File (libgphoto2)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Fetches a partial, large picture file from the camera. This command (0x9022) accepts three arguments, including specific parameters like size and format (JPEG indicated). It's designed for retrieving large image data efficiently.

```c
/* Opcode: 0x9022 */
/* Arguments: 3 */
/* Argument values (example): 80 05 00 57, 00 00 00 00, c2 b8 07 00 */
/* Command: getbigpartialpictfile */
/* Response format: 4 byte size, JPEG */
// 0x9022: 4 byte size, JPEG
```

00000000: 0c 00 00 00 01 00 10 91 34 00 00 00
00000000: 30 00 00 00 02 00 10 91 34 00 00 00 24 00 00 00
00000010: 15 d1 00 00 44 65 74 69 20 46 6c 69 65 67 6c 20
00000020: 30 30 34 39 31 35 31 31 37 38 36 37 34 38 30 00

### GET /gphoto2/settings/{setting_name}

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/canon-eos760d.txt

Retrieves the current value of a specific camera setting.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto2/settings/{setting_name}

### Description
Retrieves the current value of a specific camera setting.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto2/settings/{setting_name}

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **setting_name** (string) - The name of the setting to retrieve (e.g., "datetime", "reviewtime", "capturetarget").

### Request Example

None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **setting** (object) - Information about the requested setting.
  - **label** (string) - The human-readable label of the setting.
  - **type** (string) - The data type of the setting (e.g., "DATE", "RADIO", "TEXT").
  - **current_value** (any) - The current value of the setting.
  - **printable_value** (string, optional) - A human-readable representation of the current value (e.g., for DATE type).
  - **choices** (array of objects, optional) - Available choices for RADIO type settings.
    - **id** (integer) - The identifier for the choice.
    - **label** (string) - The label for the choice.
  - **help** (string, optional) - Help text for the setting.

#### Response Example
**Example for Camera Date and Time:**
```json
{
  "setting": {
    "label": "Camera Date and Time",
    "type": "DATE",
    "current_value": 1437908681,
    "printable_value": "Sun Jul 26 12:04:41 2015",
    "help": "Use 'now' as the current time when setting."
  }
}
```

**Example for Quick Review Time:**
```json
{
  "setting": {
    "label": "Quick Review Time",
    "type": "RADIO",
    "current_value": "2 seconds",
    "choices": [
      { "id": 0, "label": "None" },
      { "id": 1, "label": "2 seconds" },
      { "id": 2, "label": "4 seconds" },
      { "id": 3, "label": "8 seconds" },
      { "id": 4, "label": "Hold" }
    ]
  }
}
```
```

### Get Camera Status API

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sigma-fp.txt

Fetches the status of the camera, including directory information and file details. It returns structured data about the camera's state.

```APIDOC
## GET /gphoto2/camerastatus

### Description
Retrieves comprehensive status information about the camera, including details about directories and file structures.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gphoto2/camerastatus

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **args** (string) - Optional - A comma-separated string of arguments for getcamstatus2, typically "0x0,0x0,0x0".

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **camera_status** (object) - An object containing camera status details, including:
  - **length** (dword) - The total length of the status data.
  - **nrofdirs** (dword) - The number of directories.
  - **dirs** (array) - An array of directory objects, each containing:
    - **tagtype** (word) - The type of the tag.
    - **datatype** (word) - The data type of the tag.
    - **count** (dword) - The count of elements.
    - **valueoffset** (dword) - The offset to the value.

### Response Example
```json
{
  "camera_status": {
    "length": "0x44 bytes",
    "nrofdirs": 10,
    "dirs": [
      {
        "tagtype": "0x1234",
        "datatype": "0x5678",
        "count": 5,
        "valueoffset": "0x1000"
      }
    ]
  }
}
```
```

```bash
gphoto2 --abilities
Abilities for camera             : USB PTP Class Camera

Serial port support              : no
USB support                      : yes
Capture choices                  :
                                 : Image
                                 : Preview
Configuration support            : yes
Delete selected files on camera  : yes
Delete all files on camera       : no
File preview (thumbnail) support : yes
File upload support              : yes
```

--------------------------------

### Get Image (libgphoto2 Protocol)

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/konica/qm150.txt

Initiates the transfer of an image from the camera. The process involves receiving an initial ACK or error byte, followed by image data chunks and checksums. The client must acknowledge checksums to ensure data integrity. The transfer concludes with a status byte indicating completion or the need for further transmission.

```protocol
0x1B 0x47 0x46 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X 0x3X (ESC GF xxxx)
```

### Get Storage Information

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sony-nex-5n.txt

Retrieves information about the storage devices connected to the camera, such as memory cards.

```APIDOC
## GET /api/storage

### Description
Retrieves information about the storage devices connected to the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/api/storage

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **storage_id** (string) - Identifier for the storage device (e.g., "store_00010001").
- **storage_description** (string) - Description of the storage device.
- **volume_label** (string) - The volume label of the storage device.
- **storage_type** (string) - The type of storage (e.g., "Removable RAM (memory card)").
- **filesystem_type** (string) - The filesystem type of the storage.
- **access_capability** (string) - The access capability of the storage (e.g., "Read-Only").
- **maximum_capability** (string) - The total capacity of the storage device.
- **free_space_bytes** (string) - The amount of free space in bytes.
- **free_space_images** (string) - The amount of free space in terms of images (-1 if not applicable).

#### Response Example

{
  "storage_id": "store_00010001",
  "storage_description": "Storage Media",
  "volume_label": "",
  "storage_type": "Removable RAM (memory card)",
  "filesystem_type": "Generic Hierarchical",
  "access_capability": "Read-Only",
  "maximum_capability": "31092375552 (29652 MB)",
  "free_space_bytes": "31020056576 (29583 MB)",
  "free_space_images": "-1"
}
```

### Parse XML Strings in C

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/olympus.txt

Demonstrates the usage of the `parse_xml` function to parse various XML strings representing camera data and configurations. These examples showcase different XML structures for output, input, and specific camera codes.

```c
parse_xml ("<?xml version=\"1.0\"?><x3c xmlns=\"http://www1.olympus-imaging.com/ww/x3c"><output><result>2001</result><c910A><param>00000001</param></c910A></output></x3c>\n");
parse_xml ("<?xml version=\"1.0\"?><x3c xmlns=\"http://www1.olympus-imaging.com/ww/x3c"><output><result>2001</result><c1014><p5007><type>0004</type><attribute>01</attribute><default>017C</default><value>0230</value><enum>017C 0190 01C2 01F4 0230 0276 02C6 0320 0384 03E8 044C 0514 0578 0640 0708 07D0 0898</enum></p5007></c1014></output></x3c>");
parse_xml ("<?xml version=\"1.0\"?><x3c xmlns=\"http://www.olympus-imaging.com/ww/x3c"> <output> <result>2001</result> <c1015> <pD10E> <value>00000000</value> </pD10E> </c1015> </output> </x3c>");
parse_xml ("<?xml version=\"1.0\"?><x3c xmlns=\"http://www.olympus-imaging.com/ww/x3c"><input><eC102><p5018/><pD126/><p5013/><pD104/><p500C/><pD106/><pD159/><pD103/><pD15C/><pD10E/></eC102></input></x3c>");
```

### Description

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/main/settings/datetime

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **value** (string or integer) - The desired date and time. Use 'now' for the current time, or a Unix timestamp.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "value": "now"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **Status** (string) - Indicates success or failure of the operation.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "Status": "OK"
}
```

## GET /main/imgsettings/imageformat

### Description
Retrieves the current image format setting.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/main/imgsettings/imageformat

### Parameters
None

### Request Example
None

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **Current** (string) - The current image format (e.g., "Large Normal JPEG").
- **Choices** (array of objects) - Available image format options.
  - **Value** (integer) - The value representing the choice.
  - **Label** (string) - The descriptive label for the choice.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "Current": "Large Normal JPEG",
  "Choices": [
    { "Value": 0, "Label": "RAW" },
    { "Value": 1, "Label": "Large Fine JPEG" },
    { "Value": 2, "Label": "Large Normal JPEG" },
    { "Value": 3, "Label": "Medium Normal JPEG" },
    { "Value": 4, "Label": "Small Normal JPEG" },
    { "Value": 5, "Label": "Large Fine JPEG+RAW" },
    { "Value": 6, "Label": "Large Normal JPEG+RAW" },
    { "Value": 7, "Label": "Medium Normal JPEG+RAW" },
    { "Value": 8, "Label": "Small Normal JPEG+RAW" }
  ]
}
```

### EOS_GetSupport PTP Command in Python

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/canon-eos-discovery.md

This example retrieves camera support information using the PTP command 0x913f. It calls the transaction function with the command code and specifies no data phase. The response is stored in the model_id variable.

```python
model_id = ptp_obj.transaction( 0x913f, [], False )
```

### PTP Opcode and Device Properties - libgphoto2

Source: https://github.com/gphoto/libgphoto2/blob/master/camlibs/ptp2/cameras/sony-qx30u.txt

This section defines PTP opcodes and enumerates device properties with their read/write status, type, and current values. It includes camera control actions like S2_Button, Media_Format, AE_Lock, and camera settings like Camera_Setting_Reset and Camera_Initialize. This is crucial for understanding camera command structures.

```text
S2_Button(0xd617):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Media_Format(0xd61c):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
S1_Button(0xd61d):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
AE_Lock(0xd61e):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Property 0xd630:(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Power_Off(0xd637):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
AF_Lock(0xd63b):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Zoom_Tele(0xd63c):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Zoom_Wide(0xd63e):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Focus_Near_For_One_Shot(0xd6a1):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Focus_Far_For_One_Shot(0xd6a2):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Focus_Near_For_Continuous(0xd6a3):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Focus_Far_For_Continuous(0xd6a4):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Property 0xd6a5:(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Camera_Setting_Reset(0xd6d9):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
Camera_Initialize(0xd6da):(readwrite) (type=0x4) Enumeration [1,2] value: 1
```
